<div id="tr1203722"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1203722"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
According to Star Wars canon, Obi-Wan's hanging braid is a Jedi tradition common to all Padawan Learners. When his Master feels that he has reached proper maturity, he cuts the braid with his lightsaber, signifying that the student is now a full Jedi Knight.  </div>

<div id="tr0795554"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795554"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> convinced <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> to keep a scene where Qui-Gon Jinn puts his hand on Shmi Skywalker's shoulder. Lucas felt this might be out of character for the monk-like Jedi, but Neeson thought there should be an emotional connection between the characters. In an interview with Premiere magazine, Neeson defended his action, saying, "It may be 'Star Wars', but we've got to have something in there for the adults."  </div>

<div id="tr1652164"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1652164"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0005157">Jake Lloyd</a> has said that he retired from acting because of the trauma he experienced after playing Anakin Skywalker. According to Lloyd, other children constantly teased him about the role. For example they would make lightsaber sounds whenever he walked by. Lloyd also said that the situation was made worse because, in his opinion, the film did not meet the fans' expectations. Despite this, Lloyd has reprised the role of Anakin in several video games and has appeared at Star Wars conventions/events.  </div>

  <div class="sodatext">
The sound of the underwater monsters growling near the beginning of the film was made by the main sound technician's three-year-old daughter. The sound of her crying was recorded, and the frequency lowered to obtain the sound heard in the film.  </div>

<div id="tr2463776"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2463776"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the Galactic Senate scene, when Queen Amidala is asking for a vote of no confidence, and the whole Senate are on their feet shouting, in the lower left corner you can see that there are E.T. species (as in movie <a href="/title/tt0083866">E.T. the Extra-Terrestrial</a> (1982)). George Lucas included them, as a tribute to his long-time friend, Steven Spielberg, as well as showing them existing in the same universe.  </div>

<div id="tr0795073"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795073"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
At the time of the film's release, the producers ran a disinformation campaign to suggest that <a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a> played both Padmé and The Queen at all times. In fact, they are not always the same person. For many sections of the film, notably those where The Queen is wearing the black outfit with the huge feather headdress, she is actually a decoy, played by <a href="/name/nm0461136">Keira Knightley</a>. The real queen, Portman, is actually disguised as a handmaiden. Various conflicting public statements make it extremely difficult to figure out who is who. Whole websites are devoted to figuring out which actress is playing which handmaiden or The Queen at any given point.  </div>

<div id="tr2085192"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2085192"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000637">Tupac Shakur</a> (a Star Wars fan since childhood) expressed interest in reading for a role, even lobbying mutual friends of his and George Lucas' to get them in touch with each other to set up a meeting so he could read but his tragic murder in September 1996 prevented any such meeting from taking place. It has been speculated that he was up for the part of Mace Windu, but the character name was not publicly known before filming started, and it was not specifically written for an African-American until <a href="/name/nm0000168">Samuel L. Jackson</a> was cast. In early concept art, Windu was drawn as an alien and also with the likeness of Concept Designer <a href="/name/nm0156956">Doug Chiang</a>.  </div>

<div id="tr2015576"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2015576"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
A few USC students took the Japanese LaserDisc and made their own edit of the movie. Contrary to popular belief, it does NOT cut out all scenes featuring Jar-Jar Binks, but does remove many of his sillier and more distracting moments, and makes many other minor tweaks. It became known as the "Phantom Edit". <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> requested to see a copy, and then Lucasfilm issued a press release reiterating that it is illegal to copy and/or edit a Lucasfilm property.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr2015576"
class="interesting-count-text" > 130 of 135 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr0795538"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795538"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Scenes of straightforward dialogue may be comprised of up to six layers of computer-composited imagery, as the following example shows. In one scene, <a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a>'s best take had been take seven while <a href="/name/nm0005157">Jake Lloyd</a>'s was take one. The two takes were spliced together. However, Lloyd's mouth at the end of the scene is still gaped open, so the same segment from take fifteen (in which his mouth is closed) is patched in. Furthermore, when Portman appears to look down from Lloyd instead of up, those few seconds were run backwards, which unexpectedly caused steam in the background to rise in reverse. The problem was fixed by flipping the steam backwards. All these fixes resulted in a seamless scene. This technique prompted <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a>, upon the film's release, to complain thus, "We are basically puppets. I don't think I can live with the inauthenticity of movies anymore."  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr0795538"
class="interesting-count-text" > 168 of 176 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr0795350"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795350"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> made a similar deal as he did in the original <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977). Lucas and 20th Century Fox agreed that he would forego his salary as a director, provided he owns the entire negative of the final cut of the film, as well as ancillary rights of all toys and commercial tie-ins.  </div>

<div id="tr0795612"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795612"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In 1997, a fierce sandstorm destroyed several of the Tatooine sets in the desert outside Tozeur, Tunisia. Filming resumed two days later. <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> considered this a good omen, as the very same thing had happened during filming of the original <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977).  </div>

The name used by the Queen while in disguise (and, later, after her term as Queen ends), "Padmé", is the Sanskrit word for "lotus". "Yoda" is also derived from the Sanskrit word for "warrior".  </div>

<div id="tr0795303"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795303"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Earlier drafts of the script placed more emphasis on the character of Obi-Wan Kenobi. Originally, he was already a fully trained Jedi by the start of the movie, and also the only Jedi negotiator sent to Naboo. In this same draft, the character of Qui-Gon Jinn was not introduced until the characters reached Coruscant, and that character was of the same age of Obi-Wan, not his mentor.  </div>

Dates in Star Wars are based around the Battle of Yavin (in <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977)): <ul><li><a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999) takes place 32 years BBY (Before the Battle of Yavin),</li><br /><br /><li><a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002) is 22 BBY,</li><br /><br /><li><a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005) is 19 BBY,</li><br /><br /><li><a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977): is 0 BBY,</li><br /><br /><li><a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980) is 3 years ABY (After the Battle of Yavin),</li><br /><br /><li><a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983) is 4 ABY.</li><br /><br /></ul>  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr0794969"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0794969"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Palpatine's line "There is no civility, there is only politics" is a corruption of part of the Jedi Code which consists of a negative assertion followed by a positive one. For example: "There is no fear, there is only calm. There is no death, there is only the Force."  </div>

<div id="tr0795465"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795465"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the original trilogy, lightsaber activations and deactivations happened off-screen most of the time to prevent the "jumps" that would occur when the film was stopped to allow the "activated" lightsaber props to be substituted for the deactivated handles. This no longer poses a problem and every activation/deactivation occurs on-screen in this film.  </div>

<div id="tr0795512"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795512"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Qui-Gon Jinn identifies the Queen's starship as a Nubian model J-327. "327" was the number of the landing bay where the Millennium Falcon landed on the first Death Star in <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977) as well as the number of the landing platform in Cloud City in <a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980).  During the introduction of the pod racers, one of the pods is "327".  </div>

  <div class="sodatext">
According to <a href="/name/nm0078886">Ahmed Best</a> in a Rolling Stone article, <a href="/name/nm0001391">Michael Jackson</a> "campaigned" for the role of Jar Jar Binks, but <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided against casting him, because his star status would "compromise" the film. At one point, Lucas took Best and <a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a> backstage at a concert, and introduced Best to Jackson to gain the singer's approval.  </div>

<div id="tr1339450"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1339450"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The announcer at the Pod Race welcomes people, "...from all the Outer Rim Territories." This is a reference to the galaxy's grouping. The Star Wars galaxy is organized in concentric circles. Starting at the center and moving outward the circles are, The Deep Core, Core, Colonies, Inner Rim, Expansion Region, Mid Rim, Outer Rim, Wild Space, Unknown Regions.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr1649661"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1649661"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In both of his identities, Darth Sidious/Palpatine makes his first appearance as a hologram. This is in keeping with the original trilogy, when his first appearance was a holographic communication with Darth Vader in <a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980).  </div>

<div id="tr1998283"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1998283"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The interiors of the palace on Naboo were shot in an Italian palace, the Reggia Reale (Royal Palace) of Caserta (now used mostly as a museum). However, the palace had candelabras on the wall which had to be removed prior to shooting. One of the curators, there to watch that the crew doesn't make damages, played one of Amidala's counselors.  </div>

<div id="tr2752818"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752818"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0005157">Jake Lloyd</a> retired from acting in 2001, citing bullying on the part of classmates, and the stress of doing up to sixty interviews a day, as his reasons for doing so. He stated in a 2012 interview, that being in the film, ruined his childhood and his acting career, and that he destroyed all of his Star Wars memorabilia out of anger toward the film. However, an interview with a Star Wars fansite has confirmed, that he's mellowed out since then, and contrary to popular belief, he does not hate Star Wars after all the bullying.  </div>

  <a name="tr2752847"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Regarding some rumors saying that he "felt like a puppet while working on the film, <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> said, "That's simply not true," and that he had "absolutely no misgivings" about being in it, adding that <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> was "very good" to work with. "He was clear about what he wanted," said Neeson.  </div>

<div id="tr0795630"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795630"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a>'s very first draft of <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977) began, "This is the story of Mace Windu, a revered Jedi-bendu of Opuchi who was related to Usby C.J. Thape, a padawan learner of the famed Jedi." Both the character of Mace Windu and the concept of padawan learners make their first appearance in <a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999).  </div>

C-3P0 was originally only supposed to appear in scenes set in, and around the slave quarters. During post-production, <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided to optically add the droid to several outside scenes.  </div>

<div id="tr0795373"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795373"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
"Phantom Menace" was the name of a villain in the "Flash Gordon" comics. The same name used by NASA to refer to the fact that so few of their attempts to send a probe to Mars, were successful, to the point that the missions seemed cursed.  </div>

<div id="tr0795146"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795146"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
When Palpatine lands at Naboo at the end of the film, he's accompanied by Senate Guards dressed in blue. The guards' costumes are similar to those of the red Emperor's guards seen in <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002), <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005), and <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983), and are, in a way, predecessors to the later red guards.  </div>

<div id="tr2477688"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2477688"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a> worked extensively with a voice coach on what kind of dialect Queen Amidala would have. They settled on a classically imperious kind of tone, the type that <a href="/name/nm0000031">Katharine Hepburn</a> or <a href="/name/nm0000002">Lauren Bacall</a> would have used in their heyday. Portman's voice was then electronically lowered in post-production to make her sound more queenly.  </div>

<div id="tr2291851"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2291851"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
On his way to England to be fitted for the suit of Jar Jar Binks, <a href="/name/nm0078886">Ahmed Best</a> suffered severe burns when hot tea was spilled into his lap. Best endured great pain while a cast of his body was made, but told no one about his injury, unwilling to take any chance that might jeopardize his role.  </div>

<div id="tr0795488"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795488"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> asked <a href="/name/nm0001410">Lawrence Kasdan</a> to write the script (and possibly for <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002) and <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005) as well), but he turned it down, because he thought with <a href="/title/tt0080684">Star Wars: Episode V - The Empire Strikes Back</a> (1980) and <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983), Lucas's relationship to the movies had taken one step back, and that he alone should take responsibility, and make exactly the movie he wanted to make.  </div>

<div id="tr2463659"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2463659"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the Senate scene, one of the pods contains creatures that resemble E.T., an obvious tribute to <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a>' friend, <a href="/name/nm0000229">Steven Spielberg</a>. Author James Luceno fleshed out this group of aliens in his Star Wars novel, "Cloak of Deception." They are from the planet Brodo Asogi, and they are represented by Senator Greblieps (Spielberg spelled backwards.)  </div>

<div id="tr0795611"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795611"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The Neimodians were originally to be computer generated creatures, but to save costs, they were changed into men wearing masks. Animatronic Model Designer <a href="/name/nm0178846">John Coppinger</a> quickly recycled animatronic masks from <a href="/title/tt0119116">The Fifth Element</a> (1997), to use as the basis for their facial movements.  </div>

While <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> did the majority of his own stunts, he did have three stunt doubles on hand to do everything else. <a href="/name/nm1741713">Andrew Lawden</a> doubled for Neeson for part of the Darth Maul duel on Tatooine, while <a href="/name/nm0332980">Joss Gower</a> played Qui-Gon for some shots in the main duel near the end. <a href="/name/nm0408449">Rob Inch</a> did everything else.  </div>

<div id="tr0795622"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795622"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The words chanted during the "Duel of the Fates" are from <a href="/name/nm0336345">Robert Graves</a>' poem "The White Goddess". "The White Goddess" is a translation of the original version, "Cad Goddeu" or "The Battle of Achren", an early Celtic work of great antiquity also known as "The Battle of the Trees," which was originally composed by Gwion and is found in the "Book of Taliesin", a Thirteenth Century Welsh manuscript . <a href="/name/nm0002354">John Williams</a> had the lines "Under the tongue root a fight most dread, and another raging, behind, in the head" translated into Sanskrit. The translation sung in the movie is as follows: "Korah Matah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Rahtamah Yoodhah Korah Korah Syahdho Rahtahmah Daanyah Korah Keelah Daanyah Nyohah Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Syadho Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Daanyah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Daanyah Korah Rahtahmah Nyohah Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Syadho Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Korah Matah Korah Rahtahmah Korah Daanyah Korah Rahtahmah Nyohah Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Syadho Keelah Korah Rahtahmah Korah".  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr0795622"
class="interesting-count-text" > 77 of 90 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr0794973"

  <a name="tr0794973"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The Battle Droids were originally supposed to be as white as the Stormtroopers from the original trilogy. During pre-production, <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided to change them to beige.  </div>

<div id="tr0795431"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795431"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0781181">Andy Secombe</a> based his vocal performance of Watto on <a href="/name/nm0000027">Alec Guinness</a>' performance as Fagin in <a href="/title/tt0040662">Oliver Twist</a> (1948). So essentially, Anakin is passed from one Alec Guinness impersonator to another through the course of the film.  </div>

<div id="tr0795499"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795499"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In earlier drafts, the name of the planet where Queen Amidala comes from was called Utapau. This name was also used and abandoned in the early-1970s drafts of <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977), and was finally used for the sinkhole planet where Obi-Wan confronts General Grievous in <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005).  </div>

<div id="tr0795641"

  <a name="tr0795641"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the German language version of the film, the collaborating Trade Federation leaders have a French accent, while in the Italian language version they have heavy Russian accents. They also have Russian accents in the Czech version, except for the Viceroy, who speaks fluent Czech for reasons unknown.  </div>

<div id="tr0795479"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795479"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The name "Qui-Gon" derives from an ancient Chinese system of alternative medicine, called "Qigong". The "Jinn" part refers to the "Djinn" or genies of Arabian myth.  </div>

<div id="tr2028299"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2028299"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Early treatments of the film did not have Qui-Gon Jinn, and simply had Obi-Wan by himself, as a Jedi Knight. Qui-Gon was added as Obi-Wan's Master, to flow with the generational "Passing the Torch" theme found throughout the whole saga.  </div>

<div id="tr2752845"

  <a name="tr2752845"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> originally wanted to cast an American actor as Qui-Gon Jinn, but cast <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a>, because he considered that Neeson had great skills and presence. Lucas said Neeson was a "master actor, who the other actors will look up to, who has got the qualities of strength that the character demands".  </div>

Twelve years after the film was released, <a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> (Qui-Gon Jinn) and <a href="/name/nm0000278">Pernilla August</a> (Shmi Skywalker) both reprised their roles in <a href="/title/tt1707615">Star Wars: The Clone Wars: Overlords</a> (2011). <div id="tr0795081"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795081"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
In the summer of 1998, the movie <a href="/title/tt0120685">Godzilla</a> (1998) was released amongst a whirlwind of media hype as part an ambitious studio campaign called "Size Does Matter", featuring massive signs and banners meant to emphasize the size of the monster. After its release, the movie was the subject of an intense backlash by both critics and audiences. The programmers of www.StarWars.com put up a temporary webpage with mocking the "Godzilla" campaign with a poster lettered with the green glow reading "Plot Does Matter - May 1999", in reference to <a href="/title/tt0120915">Star Wars: Episode I - The Phantom Menace</a> (1999).  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

A puppeteer dressed in a color matching the background (in a manner similar to the Japanese puppet theater Bunraku), manipulated a skeletal C-3PO figure attached to his front, while <a href="/name/nm0000355">Anthony Daniels</a> read his lines off-camera. The puppeteer was erased from the film during post-production.  </div>

Theaters receiving the first trailer and posters were warned, in writing, to return them to the distributor (20th Century Fox) on time, or risk not receiving further media, and possibly the film itself. The "visual theme" of the planet Naboo is heavily influenced by Italian Renaissance design and architecture. While, on Tatooine, the stadium where the pod race takes place is based upon Roman designs of the early Christian era.  </div>

<div id="tr0795401"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795401"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
To fill all the Senate Pods, teams of extras (mostly Lucasfilm employees) were filmed separately. Some of them were shot on digital video. Enough library footage of Senators was gathered to populate the Senate scenes of both <a href="/title/tt0121765">Star Wars: Episode II - Attack of the Clones</a> (2002) and <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005).  </div>

The crew was considering giving the Neimoidians an alien language with subtitles, translating this into English (similar to other alien species in the franchise), but decided not to, since the Neimoidians carried the "political element" of the film, and did not want to detract from this.  </div>

<div id="tr2752837"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752837"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
As <a href="/name/nm0001068">Sofia Coppola</a> prepared the script for her directorial debut on <a href="/title/tt0159097">The Virgin Suicides</a> (1999), she heard that <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> would make a new Star Wars film, and asked him if she could accompany him during filming. Lucas offered Coppola a role in the royal entourage, which she accepted because it "seemed like a good vantage point to watch without getting in the way".  </div>

<div id="tr2816097"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2816097"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
A re-release of The Phantom Menace in 3-D, was released to theaters in February 2012. In Sweden, it was decided that the movie would also be dubbed into Swedish, despite that no other Star Wars live-action movie had been dubbed into Swedish before. Swedish actress <a href="/name/nm0000278">Pernilla August</a> who played Shmi Skywalker, did the voice-over of herself in the dub.  </div>

<div id="tr2881842"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2881842"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The beginning and end of this film also parallel the beginning and end of <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983). Both films begin with a smaller ship asking to board a larger one. Both end with the death of a Sith Lord, and the death of a Jedi, with the Jedi being given a funeral by cremation.  </div>

<div id="tr0794992"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0794992"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> approached <a href="/name/nm0002376">David Hare</a> to write the screenplay and even co-direct the film. Lucas confessed he had reservations about working with the actors, and hoped that he could focus on the action while Hare focused on the acting. Hare declined.  </div>

Before <a href="/name/nm0000168">Samuel L. Jackson</a> expressed his interest in joining the cast, Mace Windu was to be an animatronic character. <div id="tr2637843"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2637843"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
A few days before the scene, on the Royal Starship that introduces R2-D2, was to be shot, <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided that he wanted to have a 'barrel' domed droid (an R5 unit) added to the group, which was originally made up out of units with a dome similar to R2-D2. Years earlier, Lucasfilm had given away all the original R3, R4 and R5 domes to Disneyland, for their <a href="/title/tt0094029">Star Tours</a> (1987) ride, and being on location at Leavesden studios in England, <a href="/name/nm0081636">Don Bies</a> only had a single image to work with, as he quickly made an R5 dome over the weekend. Because of the rush job, it turned out looking slightly different from the original prop, but this same dome was repainted, and used, for every other R5 unit seen in all three Star War prequels.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr0795085"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795085"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0001160">Adrian Dunbar</a> was originally cast as Bail Organa, and made a brief appearance in the Senate sequence. When his performance was cut, the character's name was changed to Bail Antilles (mentioned on screen by Captain Panaka). A picture of Dunbar still appeared in two publications: The Ultimate Star Wars: Episode I Sticker Book (as Senator Bail Organa) and Star Wars: Episode I Who's Who (as Bail Antilles).  </div>

It appears that the other head of the podrace announcer is simply saying the same thing as the first head, but in Huttesse instead of English. This isn't so. <div id="tr2752822"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752822"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Nine R2-D2 models were created; one was for <a href="/name/nm0048652">Kenny Baker</a>, into which to be dropped, seven were built by ILM and featured two wheelchair motors capable of moving 440 pounds, enabling it to run, and be mostly used in stage sets, and the British studio produced a pneumatic R2-D2 that could shift from two to three legs, and was mostly used in Tunisia, because its motor-drive system allowed it to drive over sand.  </div>

<div id="tr2752829"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752829"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> decided to make elaborate costumes because the film's society was more sophisticated than the one depicted in the original trilogy. Designer <a href="/name/nm0081773">Trisha Biggar</a> and her team created over 1,000 costumes that were inspired by various cultures. Biggar worked closely with concept designer <a href="/name/nm0564572">Iain McCaig</a> to create a color palette for the inhabitants of each world: Tatooine followed <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977) with sun-bleached sand colors, Coruscant had grays, browns and blacks, and Naboo had green and gold for humans while Gungans wore "a leathery look, like their skin". The Jedi costumes followed the tradition from the original film; Obi-Wan's costume was inspired by the costume that was worn by <a href="/name/nm0000027">Alec Guinness</a>. Lucas said he and Biggar would look at the conceptual art to "translate all of these designs into cloth and fabric and materials that would actually work, and not look silly". Biggar also consulted Gillard to ensure the costumes would accommodate action scenes, and consulted the creature department to find which fabrics "wouldn't wear too heavily" on the alien skins. A huge wardrobe department was set up at Leavesden Film Studios to create over 250 costumes for the main actors and 5,000 for the background ones.  </div>

<div id="tr2752832"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752832"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> described Sebulba's design as "a spider crossed with an orangutan crossed with a sloth", with a camel-like face, and clothing inspired by medieval armor. Part of the challenge was to create a creature that used its hands as feet, and its feet as hands.  </div>

<div id="tr0795537"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795537"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Two conflicting stories have come out of Lucasfilm, on the origin of the Nemoidians' name. One version says that the the aquatically-evolved aliens were named, as an allusion to the fictional naval character, Captain Nemo. According to other sources, however, the race was named for science fiction icon <a href="/name/nm0000559">Leonard Nimoy</a>.  </div>

<div id="tr1998286"

  <a name="tr1998286"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The "buzzing" sound of Captain Panaka's portable radio is actually a "ray pistol" from the 1950s. The same sound effect was used in the original Star Wars trilogy, for the restraining bolts on droids.  </div>

<div id="tr2752823"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752823"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Editing took two years; <a href="/name/nm0809551">Paul Martin Smith</a> started the process in England and focused on dialogue-heavy scenes. <a href="/name/nm0123785">Benjamin A. Burtt</a> (who was also the film's Sound Editor) was responsible for action sequences under <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a>' supervision. Non-linear editing systems played a large part in translating Lucas' vision; he constantly tweaked, revised and reworked shots and scenes. The final sound mix was added in March 1999, and the following month the film was completed after the delivery of the remaining visual effects shots.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<a href="/name/nm0784818">Peter Serafinowicz</a> criticized <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a>' poor direction to him when voicing Darth Maul, which just amounted to "Make him sound evil." and he was not happy that only three of his lines are in the movie, and that he only got a meager salary for those lines. On top of that, he was annoyed that he wasn't even invited to the film's premiere and had to pay for his own tickets and travel expenses, and he didn't think the film was very good on top of that.  </div>

<div id="tr3130922"

  <a name="tr3130922"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Darth Maul is the only Dark Side apprentice who was not previously a Jedi. Count Dooku was once an apprentice to Yoda, and Master to Qui-Gon Jinn. Darth Vader/Anakin Skywalker is an apprentice to Obi-Wan Kenobi. Kylo Ren was an apprentice to Luke Skywalker.  </div>

<div id="tr2792079"

  <a name="tr2792079"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
During the near-fight between Sebulba and Jar Jar, a background character can be seen with light skin, dreadlocks, and yellow paint over his nose. Expanded Universe writers were inspired by this to create the character Quinlan Vos, who was later mentioned by name in <a href="/title/tt0121766">Star Wars: Episode III - Revenge of the Sith</a> (2005).  </div>

  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0698681">Greg Proops</a> and <a href="/name/nm0135750">Scott Capurro</a>, the voices of the two-headed podrace commentator, originally recorded their scenes (both in English) in full makeup in front of a greenscreen. It wasn't until the film came out, that they discovered that they had been digitally replaced. This was also when Proops realized that Capurro had separately re-recorded his lines in Huttese.  </div>

<div id="tr2814208"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2814208"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
One of the very first casting rumors for the "Star Wars Prequel", came from a science-fiction magazine called Starblazer. In their Summer 1985 issue, they published that actress <a href="/name/nm0000356">Sybil Danning</a> was to possibly portray the "sexy witch" that seduces Anakin Skywalker to the Dark Side. In 2012, Danning confirmed on her Facebook page that the rumor was indeed true, and that many discussions took place at that time.  </div>

<div id="tr2752838"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752838"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Chroma key was extensively used for digital set extensions, backgrounds, or scenes that required Cinematographer <a href="/name/nm0005897">David Tattersall</a> to seek powerful lamps to light the sets, and Visual Effects Supervisor <a href="/name/nm0461306">John Knoll</a> to develop software that would remove the blue reflection from shiny floors. Knoll, who remained on set through most of the production, worked closely with Tatterstall to ensure that the shots were suitable to add effects later.  </div>

  <a name="tr2752844"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0461306">John Knoll</a> previewed 3,500 storyboards for the film; <a href="/name/nm0000184">George Lucas</a> accompanied him to explain factors of the shots that would be practical and those which would be created through visual effects. Knoll later said that on hearing the explanations of the storyboards, he did not know how to accomplish what he had seen. The result was a mixture of original techniques and the newest digital techniques to make it difficult for the viewer to guess which technique was being used. Knoll and his visual effects team wrote new computer software, including cloth simulators to allow a realistic depiction of the digital characters' clothing, to create certain shots.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr2764584"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2764584"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
When young Anakin starts his pod racer for the first time, the ignition buttons on the panel are the same model of the Fiat Uno, an Italian car launched in 1983. One of the car's characteristics is that it featured ergonomic "pod" switchgear clusters on each side of the main instrument binnacle.  </div>

<div id="tr2073798"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2073798"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm1020089">Sally Hawkins</a> was an extra, while attending drama school. She was on set for one day, as a friend was able to give her access. She was paid 100 quid for playing an extra in the village, and wore a chiffon costume. On set she saw <a href="/name/nm0000191">Ewan McGregor</a> while he was playing football, but didn't talk to him. Years later she co-starred with him in <a href="/title/tt0795493">Cassandra's Dream</a> (2007) but has never told him they had previously "co-starred".  </div>

<div id="tr2752819"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2752819"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
To research for the podrace vehicles, the visual effects crew visited a jet aircraft junkyard outside Phoenix, Arizona and scavenged four Boeing 747 engines. Life-sized replicas of the engines were built and sent to Tunisia, to provide reference in the film.  </div>

<div id="tr3030241"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3030241"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The bullfrog in the underwater Gungan City is based on Jabba the Hut, since Jabba eats bullfrogs. He's seen in Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi eating a bucket of bullfrogs and opens the pod race in this movie by biting the head off a frog and spitting it onto the gong to start the race. Their skin tones also match the environment in which they live.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr3030241"
class="interesting-count-text" > 2 of 2 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr2752815"

  <a name="tr2752815"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The character design of Watto was an amalgam of rejected ideas; his expressions were based on video footage of <a href="/name/nm0781181">Andy Secombe</a>'s voice acting, photographs of Animation Supervisor <a href="/name/nm0171197">Rob Coleman</a> imitating the character, and Modeller Steve Alpin saying Watto's lines to a mirror.  </div>

<div id="tr3056938"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3056938"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Obi-Wan's character has many parallels to Luke in the original trilogy. Both men see their mentor cut down in front of them, and scream out "No!" in protest. Obi-Wan holds the dying Qui-Gon in his arms, just as Luke does his father. Qui-Gon makes Obi-Wan promise to train Anakin, just as Yoda implores Luke to pass on what he has learned. Neither of the two men are successful in that mission: Anakin turns to the Dark Side and becomes Darth Vader, while Luke's apprentice, Ben Solo, turns to the Dark Side and becomes Kylo Ren.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr3056938"
class="interesting-count-text" > 1 of 1 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr3235610"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3235610"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
After discovering he'd gotten the part of Obi-Wan, <a href="/name/nm0000191">Ewan McGregor</a> had his first ever lightsaber duel with <a href="/name/nm0302462">Noel Gallagher</a> using prop lightsabers owned by Noel. The duel took place in the back garden of Noel's house in Belsize Park after Ewan had attended an all-night party there the day before.  </div>

<div id="tr3056937"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3056937"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The opening sequence has parallels to both <a href="/title/tt0076759">Star Wars: Episode IV - A New Hope</a> (1977) and <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983). Like Jedi, it begins with a small ship approaching a big one, and asking for permission to board. Like A New Hope, the two main characters end up in a firefight. Qui-Gon tries to melt through the door to the bridge, just as the storm troopers cut through a door to board the Tantive IV. One major reversal is that Qui-Gon and Obi-Wan are high-ranking Jedi, while R2-D2 and C-3PO are mere droids.  </div>

<div id="tr3157570"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3157570"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
When Padmé, Anakin, Qui-Gon, and Jar Jar are seated at the table, eating at Anakin's house, the mother pours two drinks from the pitcher, for two of the glasses. The third glass, Padmé's glass, is the only one that has anything in it.  </div>

        <a id="spoilers" name="spoilers"></a>
    <h4 class="li_group">Spoilers&nbsp;</h4>
    <div class="message_box small">
        <div class="alert">
          <p>The trivia items below may give away important plot points.</p>
        </div>
    </div>
 
<div id="tr0795122"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795122"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Darth Maul only blinks once throughout the film. This is mostly because the contact lenses that <a href="/name/nm0661917">Ray Park</a> wore made it difficult to blink, and Park liked the idea of a villain who never stops staring. He blinks when he is sliced in half by Obi-Wan Kenobi.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr0795551"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr0795551"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The sound effect when Obi-Wan Kenobi's lightsaber is kicked down the reactor shaft towards the end of the movie, is the same sound effect heard when Luke Skywalker throws his lightsaber away in <a href="/title/tt0086190">Star Wars: Episode VI - Return of the Jedi</a> (1983) when he tells the Emperor that he is a Jedi.  </div>

<div id="tr2362931"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2362931"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
According to revised Star Wars canon, Darth Maul did not die when Obi-Wan sliced him in two. While falling down the pit, Maul grabbed at a maintenance hatch and swung into a disposal tube. The impact of landing knocked him out. Later, garbage collection droids dumped him into a trash bin, which was shipped to an offworld refuse dump. Maul existed there for twelve years, a broken half-mad cripple, until he was eventually rescued by his brother, Savage Oppress.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr2362931"
class="interesting-count-text" > 133 of 143 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr1075531"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr1075531"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
This is the only film in the franchise, in which the top-credited actor (<a href="/name/nm0000553">Liam Neeson</a> as Qui-Gon Jinn) plays a non-recurring character, and in which, the top-credited character dies (until Star Wars: Episode VII - The Force Awakens). Also, the only film in the prequel trilogy, that does not give Obi-Wan Kenobi (<a href="/name/nm0000191">Ewan McGregor</a>) the top credit.  </div>

<div id="tr2159186"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2159186"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
During the battle between Qui-Gon Jinn and Obi-Wan Kenobi against Darth Maul, a total of nine strikes are landed without the use of the lightsaber blade. Darth Maul lands a kick on each Jedi in the main hanger, Darth Maul lands a kick against Obi-Wan, causing him to fall to a lower platform, Qui-Gon lands an elbow and punch combination to knock Darth Maul to a lower platform, Darth Maul uses a kick as a counterattack after Qui-Gon jumps from a lower platform, Darth Maul uses the hilt of his lightsaber before fatally stabbing Qui-Gon, Obi-Wan lands a kick on Darth Maul after breaking his lightsaber in half, Darth Maul lands a kick on Obi-Wan causing him to completely flip over and land on his feet, and Darth Maul uses a force push to knock Obi-Wan into the chasm.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr3160661"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3160661"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Although this trilogy culminates with Anakin becoming Darth Vader, the main villain of the trilogy is Palpatine. That makes this trilogy the only one, in which the villain is not related to the Skywalkers. The original trilogy had Darth Vader as the primary villain, while the sequel trilogy is about his grandson, Kylo Ren.  </div>

<div id="tr3130948"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3130948"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
Qui-Gon's death forces Anakin to deal with two other Jedi: He becomes apprentice to Qui-Gon's former apprentice, Obi-Wan Kenobi. He later fights Qui-Gon's former Master, Count Dooku, loses a hand to him, then defeats him in a rematch. This is a reversal of the original trilogy, in which Obi-Wan's death forces Luke to receive training from his former Master, Yoda, and fight two duels with his former apprentice, Darth Vader.  </div>

Anakin losing his mother is a reverse of Leia trying to get away from her father (Darth Vader).  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr3018972"
class="interesting-count-text" > 5 of 12 found this interesting</a>
  <span class='interesting-cast-vote' data-item-id="tr3018972" data-item-type="trivia">
    <span>Interesting?</span>
    <button class="cast-vote" value="up">Yes</button>
    <button class="cast-vote" value="down">No</button>
  </span>
<span class="ghost">|</span>  <span class="linksoda"><a href="?item=tr3018972">Share this</a></span>
  <div class="sharesoda_pre">
    Share this: <a target="_blank"
    href="http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.imdb.com%2Ftitle%2Ftt0120915%2Ftrivia%3Fitem%3Dtr3018972"
    onclick="window.open('http://www.facebook.com/sharer.php?u=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.imdb.com%2Ftitle%2Ftt0120915%2Ftrivia%3Fitem%3Dtr3018972', 'newWindow', 'width=626,height=436'); return false;">Facebook</a>

    <a target="_blank"
    href="http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?text=Star%20Wars%3A%20Episode%20I%20-%20The%20Phantom%20Menace%20(1999)%20Trivia%20-%20http%3A%2F%2Fwww.imdb.com%2Ftitle%2Ftt0120915%2Ftrivia%3Fitem%3Dtr3018972"
    onclick="window.open('http://twitter.com/intent/tweet?status=Star%20Wars%3A%20Episode%20I%20-%20The%20Phantom%20Menace%20(1999)%20Trivia%20-%20http%3A%2F%2Fwww.imdb.com%2Ftitle%2Ftt0120915%2Ftrivia%3Fitem%3Dtr3018972', 'newWindow', 'width=815,height=436'); return false;">Twitter</a>

    &nbsp;<span class="ghost">|</span>&nbsp;
    <a href="/title/tt0120915/trivia?item=tr3018972">Permalink</a>
    <a href="#" class="hidesoda hidden">Hide&nbsp;options</a>

  </div>
</div>
<div id="tr2968189"
     class="soda even sodavote" >
  <a name="tr2968189"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The characters appear in reverse order per episode. Episode I reverses Episode IV by having Anakin arrive at 32 minutes at an indoor location compared to Luke arriving at 16 minutes in an outdoor location. Obi-Wan appears late in Episode IV, but early in Episode I. Vice versa for C-3PO. In fact, Anakin creating C-3PO foreshadows not only the fact that he will be a talking robot later in life, but Luke has it in him to be an inventor from his father, but doesn't know how to fix anything. When we first meet Luke, he's fixing a robot that is still broken. Also, his aunt and uncle say after lunch "He has a lot of his father in him." Leia also has some of her father in her. She's held captive in Episode IV as he is in I and senses things before they happen. Leia is trying to escape her father (Darth Vader) without knowing they're related, but Anakin is taken away from his mom. He loses a dream to free the slaves, but Luke gained a dream of being a Jedi, after his aunt and uncle died. R2-D2 brings a spaceship to Tatooine where Anakin appears, but would later show a hologram of Princess Leia to Luke, leading him from Tatooine to a spaceship, to save her. Therefore, he's responsible for the discovery of two slaves. Obi-Wan kills Darth Maul in Episode I, and gets killed by Darth Vader in Episode IV. Qui-Gon needed to die, so it can mirror Obi-Wan's death from Darth Vader.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">
<a href="?item=tr2968189"
class="interesting-count-text" > 3 of 7 found this interesting</a>

<div id="tr3021781"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3021781"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
The opening of Episode IV reverses in Episode I. Episode I opens with four characters approaching the spaceship, where a female Astrodroid greets the Jedi's. Soon, an explosion occurs, where white smoke in another room emerges, contrasting the dark interiors of the spaceship, where the Jedi's do battle with robots. Queen Amidala sends a message. In Episode IV, C-3PO is the first character talking, and soon Stormtroopers start blasting characters with guns, leading to an explosion of black smoke, contrasting the white interior of the spaceship, from where Darth Vader emerges. Princess Leia sends a message, and two characters (C-3PO and R2-D2) leave the spaceship.  </div>
  <div class="did-you-know-actions">

<div id="tr3222873"
     class="soda odd sodavote" >
  <a name="tr3222873"></a>
  <div class="sodatext">
<a href="/name/nm0000204">Natalie Portman</a> plays the mother of <a href="/name/nm0000402">Carrie Fisher</a>'s character. Portman's first film was <a href="/title/tt0110413">L&eacute;on: The Professional</a> (1994), in which the title character watches <a href="/title/tt0045152">Singin' in the Rain</a> (1952), which featured Fisher's real-life mother, <a href="/name/nm0001666">Debbie Reynolds</a>. Like Reynolds, Portman at one point sings the title song.  </div>
